  11. I have tried both the Crest Whitestrips Professional Effects with level 4 whitening and the Intensive Professional Effects with level 5 whitening. I have also had professional whitening done in the past through the dentist.<br /><br />I want to state up front that whitening your teeth will not be a painless process. You are putting peroxide and other whitening ingredients onto your teeth and they are made to permeate the surface. You have nerves inside your teeth and peroxide burns. Tooth and gum sensitivity is to be expected. You're bleaching your teeth. Do not whiten your teeth expecting zero sensitivity or pain. To expect that is like expecting exercise to not make your muscles really hurt when you haven't exercised them in a very long time. It's going to hurt.<br /><br />How do you deal with the sensitivity? What I do is start brushing with a toothpaste made to cut back on sensitivity at least 14 days in advance of the whitening process. Also use a mouthwash or rinse made for sensitivity as well. DO NOT BRUSH YOUR TEETH RIGHT BEFORE APPLYING ANY WHITENING PRODUCTS!! The reason for this is because when you brush your teeth you commonly get very tiny cuts in your mouth. To use whitening products too soon after brushing your teeth is basically to put peroxide directly into these tiny cuts which equals a lot more pain, and you're also directly putting the peroxide into your bloodstream which can make you sick. Wait at least an hour after brushing to apply the whitestrips. If you're worried about debris on your teeth you can rinse your mouth out with water.<br /><br />For the first few days expect a lot of tooth sensitivity. I learned to take a Tylenol in advance of applying the whitestrips and it significantly cuts down on pain. With the professional effects series of whitestrips you can drink water, but I recommend using a straw if possible because if you get the strips too wet they will start to slip and you digest some of the gel which can make you sick to yourstomach. I hydrate prior to whitening so I'm not having to guzzle water during the process.<br /><br />As far as whitening results go, I did find the Intensive professional Effects whitestrips to have the most whitening. Don't expect to get teeth as white as what you see on TV or in magazines. Unless your teeth are already white and have been whitened before professionally you aren't likely to get blinding white results. As a kid my teeth were discolored by Tetracycline, so I had my teeth professionally whitened years ago The thing is, really deep stains DO start to reappear over time so whitening is not permanent, especially if you drink coffee, soda, tea and eat staining foods. If you are a heavy soda drinker or eat a lot of acidic foods you may have enamel loss and that will also make whitening significantly less effective and whole lot more painful.<br /><br />So how do the Intensive Professional Effects whitestrips compare to the real deal professional whitening? Honestly, it's not the same, but this is the best over the counter whitening kit I have ever used, hands down. When I had my professional whitening done it cost $300, and that was just my top teeth and was back in the late 1990s, so I'm sure it would be way more expensive now. My professional whitening was syringes of peroxide gel I added to a custom fitted plastic tray that I wore twice a day for 2 hours each time. I had extraordinary results from it with all my yellow Tetracycline stains removed and my whitening was whiter than their charts. I did 3 rounds of the professional whitening system and my teeth stayed white for years, but in the past couple years I have had to touch them up.<br /><br />If your teeth are not too badly stained or you have done professional whitening before, this kit is excellent. It will save you a lot of money, time, and effort. If you have really deep stains, enamel loss, or other concerns I would recommend you save your money and get your teeth professionally whitened bya dentist. If you are concerned about pain, I would recommend you talk to your dentist and find out what whitening method would be best for you.

Plus I figured I'd save money cause with the intensive Professional Effects, you use less since they are stronger.<br /><br />Ok I ordered them and used them just like normal teeth strips and I experienced some tooth pain and severe sensitivity after about the third use and stopped using them.<br /><br />I did some more research and experimenting and i realized that the tooth paint and sensitivity is more prominent when you completely fold the strips over your entire teeth. Essentially the contact with the very tip of your teeth (where it is thinnest and where you experience the most pain/sensitivity) is a large part of the problem. So after the fourth use I started cutting the individual strips in half and applying them JUST on the front and back of each row of teeth. I did not completely encase the teeth in the strip and essentially left the very tips/points of my teeth uncovered by the strips. I still get the full benefits of the whitening...BUT I EXPERIENCE LITTLE TO ABSOLUTELY NO TOOTH PAIN!!!<br /><br />This is extremely important: If you want to use these or even strong strips without experiencing tooth pain or hightened sensitivity, DO NOT ALLOW THE STRIPS TO COMPLETELY COVER/ENCASE YOUR TEETH. Cut or apply the whitening strips such that the crowns of your teeth are exposed. In my experience it is mostly when the crowns of your teeth are covered by the strips for the 2 hour time period is what mostly triggers the tooth pain. And no I didnt use sensodine or any other products to reduce the pain/sensitivity - I just cut the strips so that they completely cover the front and don't folder over to the backsides of my teeth. Doing this has made using these strips for the recommended period of time bearable.

I thought for a long time that the pain I endured from whitening my teeth was something that I just had to put up with. I don't think I'm &#34;used&#34; to teeth sensitivity, but it's more of my method of dealing with sensitivity: I use FLUORIDE mouthwash (from Crest; it tastes delicious and has no burn) and let my sensitive teeth 'soak' in the solution. Meaning I don't 'swish swish spit', I just keep it in my mouth until my sensitivity goes away. I think this thoroughly kills whatever is ailing my teeth and allows my gums to heal. The thing about teeth sensitivity is that it's due to the dentin tubules (whichlie under the enamel) being exposed. So your dentin nerves could be exposed due to receding gums or even worn down enamel. In my case, I think it's receding gums so I do what I can to encourage my nerves to grow back.<br /><br />That's why I use fluoride mouthwash; fluoride makes the dentin less permeable, hardens the enamel, and allows the gums to regenerate. Teeth whitening can soften your enamel a bit so harden it back up with some fluoride. Don't brush your teeth immediately after whitening, but a mouthwash should do your mouth some good without any mechanical abrasion on your teeth. Basically, before and after whitening, do what you can to put your teeth in prime condition and the sensitivity should be lessened. You could use sensodyne and maybe even some pain relievers, but personally, I prefer to rid the source of the pain rather than suppress the pain.<br /><br />Also make sure you do not get these strips on your gums! Hydrogen peroxide is cytotoxic meaning it's toxic to cells and you're wearing this for two hours! Protect those gums otherwise you're going to give your teeth a reason to give you more hell when you're whitening along with aching gums.<br /><br />I'll be updating this review in four days. :D

Worse yet, as I mentioned, is the anticipation of the pain...the knowing that at some point, you're going to get this rather uncomfortable pain in you mouth! I noticed the pain bursts were less intense and less frequent than the first day...but that definitely goes against what I was reading online.<br /><br />Day 3 was the last day I'd use the strips in consecutive days; I went on the road to visit friends and family across the state, and used the strips during the 7 hour drive. Almost no effect whatsoever! Very little pain, very little discomfort, and I really could tell the difference. I could have hot and cold foods/beverages without a problem. Staying out of my house got me out of the daily routine, so I skipped a day, then put them back in for day 4. No big deal. I skipped a few days, and put in the 5th application...no big deal. Skipped a few more days, and finally got around to putting in the 6th trip when I got back home today. Figured I'd wear them on my run. I made it about 5 minutes (still stretching for my run!) before I had to take them out. It was a terrible pain, and maybe I felt like I'd had enough, but I said hell with it. I got 5 days of 2hrs in, no more discomfort!<br /><br />My teeth look good...I have a special toothpaste to remineralize the teeth and to hopefully add to the whitening process, while desensitizing them from the whitening process. All in all, it does what it says. It whitens for sure. It hurts for sure. However, their big selling point is time, whereas even as a teacher with the summer off, I found it difficult to stay on track and follow through with it for 7 days. I never experienced pain when the strips were off, unlike many other reviewers, but be aware, the pain can really knock your socks off at times! Good luck!
